JOSEPH D. CHARLES
Joseph D. Charles, a Negro, was born 15 November 1907, at
Limbe, Haiti. He is married and has five children. He received
his law degree at the Law School in Cap Hatien in 1928. A for-
mer law professor, Assistant Prosecuting Attorney and Judge of
the Civil Court in Cap Hatien (1928 - 1940); Charles served as
Ambassador to the United States from 8 October 1946 until 1 June
1960. During this period, he served also as Ambassador on the
Council of the Organization of American States (1949 - 1950).
He resigned his ambassadorial post after the fall of the gove
ment of President Estime who had appointed him. On 29 February
1952, ho was designated Secretary of Education and Public Works
by President Magloire and resigned from the cabinet on 31 March
1953, allegedly because of his opposition to increasingly close
ties between the governments of Haiti and the Dominican Republic.
Charles chaired the Haitian delegation to the second post of
the first session of the UN General Assembly (1946), the second
session (1947) and the fourth session (1949). He chaired also
the delegation to the Ninth International Conference of American
States at Bogata (1948) and is reported to have been friendly to
the United States.
Charles has in the past been mentioned. more than once as a
possible successor to the incumbent president. The most recent
occasion was in 1953 when he was menticead as a possible successor
to President Paul E. Magloire.

- 2
CHARLES
Madame Chorles, nee Telson, is a sister of Adelphin Telson,
formerly Minister of Defense and Justice, formerly President of
the Chamber of Deputies, who is friendly to the US and in con-
tact with US officials in Port-au-Prince A sister of Madame
Charles is married to Colonel Marcaisse Prosper, former Chief
of Police under the Magloire government. It has been alleged
that the three men, Charles, Telson and Presper, constitute a
potentially strong political force in Haiti.

1999
IX-104
30 April 1963
CONTACT REPORT
WUBRINY - Haitian Operation
1. WUBRINY/1 telephuned from his residence on the sterile
lims at approximately 0930 hours to report the following.
2. WUBRINY/1 said that he believed that the meeting that
is to be held by Mr. CHARLES and WUBRINY/1 plus an unmanual third
party would involve a Mr. Tardieu.
3. I told WUBRINY/1 there had been considerable interest
in this general development on the part of the Department of
State and cited (without identification) A-406, Amambassy, Port-
au-Prince, dated April 11, 1963, subject: U.S. Businessman Signs
Contracts with Haitian Government and Local Bank. I told WUBRINY/1
that the 1963 and said that the American Association was relevant
to the 13, 1963 and said that the A1grane also mentioned a
Mr. Rert Cindine TARDIEU. I also gave WUBRINY/1 the points raised
under "comme-nt" on page 2 of the A1gram.
4. WUBRINY/1 said that he agreed with all of these comments
as he had come to the same conclusione.
5. I told WUBRINY/1 that there was obviously considerable
interesr in any reporting that he can do on this subject and
requested that he let me know when the meeting takes place and
continue his detailed reporting as heretofore. He agreed to do so.
C. FRANK STUNE, III
Chief

If the competitive communities are so dynamic and impose by the rate of their
dysle of evolution, it is because, to the end, their social struggles result into
economic terms through the production of valuable men superior to their consumption.
Because we failed to draw up our balance-sheet at each epoch of our life, we do
not seem to understand that we are arriving at inverse reports. Our bchavranese is
the result of this negative unbalance between the production and the consumption of
our valuable men.
We should be concious of the urgency if not to change our method of struggling, at
least to come up with superior principles susceptible of making our struggles less
naive and such more profitable to the community. On this point, the example offered
by more advanced countries of which we are copying the bad aides can be of service
to us. To decrease the rate of consumption of our valuable men in order to increase
their production in the course of time is to lewn to appreciate, then to utilise
and to respect them. We shall, thereby, exace the condition that will preserve and
focundate them.
We know, indeed, that it is extremely hard to come to this reasoning, it is me
more difficult to adopt it as the note of our collective behavior. We are only a
few to grasp this thruth because this phase of our social competitions results inte
a
mess of historic factors. The first effect of our internal diviaions generated by
celenicilism and fed up, afterwards by the old regime of oppression was the section,
at the various levels of our societies of a complex of self destruction, that turned
into a social cannibalism. In the production of this event where everyone, without
undergoing in any way the influence of a systic or of a superior principle, is moved
while believing he is moving taverde his rightful interest, one has the impression

MR. CLELARD JOSER CHENES
COE- 3,260 843
President & General Kinnager, Banque Commerziale d'Haiti, Fort-au-Frinoe.
Life Story
Born at Connives, Haiti, on April 21, 1923, of peasant parents; vent
to Parochial Sobholl; in 1939 graduated from Lyode Oeffrard, Conaives; taught
in rural schools; in addition, father having died in 1939, did various jobs
to support his family, symboloterer, time-keeper, plantation supervisor,
free lance journalist, etc.
In 1947, appointed Controler General of Aeytian Southern Banana Industry;
became General Agent in 1948.
In 1949 established himself as Kanufasturers' Representative and created
his own export and import business.
In 1953 vent to London as Member of the Economic Mission of the
Haytian Government, and in 1954 negotiated on the Aeytian Government's
behalf a contract with the General Kioetrio Co.Ltd., of Coventry, England
for the modernising and extending of the telecommunition system in Haiti.
In 1957, appointed Member of the Haytian Mission to the International
Conference held in Brussels, Belgium.
In 1960 created the Banque Commerciale d'Haiti.
Mx. Charles is the sole owner of the Banque Commerciale d'Haiti and
the full or part owner of several industrial and commercial enterprises
in Haiti, such as :
Universal Enterprises Co.,B.A.) (U.B.A.C.O.)
National Deutsch Associates, S.A., - Cienard Joseph Charles Imperes-Emper
Greece Industry in the Eorth - Cienard Jueema Charles & Co.
News Charles & Co.
Ne is the cale Representetive in Haiti of the following commence :
The General Electric Co.Ltd., London, England
Siemens Echukert Kerske, Geman
Bank References :
Ehagus Ationale de la Republique d'Haiti
Fort-u-Frinoe, Haiti
The Royal Bank of Canada, New York
Zoving Trust Company, New York
Nember of :
The Committee for the Rehabilitation of the Rural Ecetions of Haiti
the Retitan Chamber of Commerce
The International Club of Commerce, Haiti
Commerces & Industry Association of New York - Charter Membes
Batesy Club, Fert-au-Frinoe, Tembe Club of Fert-au-Frinoe.

CURRICULUM VITAE
Hore in Conieves, Haiti, on April 21, 1923, from a ponsant finally.
End his primary schooling at the "Ecole des Freres des Conalves,"
and his secondary schooling at the "Lyde Ceffrard' in the same tonn.
Upon his father's death, did various jobs to support his family.
Was in turn schoolmester at the rural school of Verrrettes, at $15
a month, free lance teacher at $0.40 per month per child, time-
becquer, plantation supervisor, photographe, sanitary clerk, free
fance journalist. In the latter capacity, founded 'L' 'Interjudice' and
L' 'Maurer' in cooperation with the late Emmanuel C. Paul.
Fyto-Fethologist.
In 1946, uss appointed Controller General of the Bennas Development
Company (BADECO), of which he became the General Ascent in 1948.
The following year, established himself as Manufacturez's Agent,
and created an Import-Export trade house.
Married in 1952, Sophie Mieriseon.
In 1953, went to Lenkton as a Member of the Economic Mission sent to
England by the Haitian Government, and in 1954, negotiated, on behalf
of the Government, a contract with The General Electric Co., Ltd.,
Overwarty, England. This contract was in connection with the extension
and modernisation of the Telecommunication System in Haiti.
In 1977, the appointed as a member of the Economic Mission to the
International Conference held in Brussels, Belgium.
Created in 1960, the 'BARQUE CONVERSICIALE D'HAETI,' of which he is
the President and Director General. In also the President of the
following firms he himself created:

SUBJECT

APPROXISAL UNITED STATES CITIZEN (C) WHO GRANATES A BUSINESS IN HAITI, WHERE HE EYJOS
THE FIFNISHIP OF MANT MILITARY AND GOVERNMENT LEADERS, AND WHO IS A FORMER
MILITARY OFFICER AND A TRAINED REPORTER, FROM SAUDERS V. ROBERSON.
APPRISAL: 3.
1. OH OR ABOUT 3 OCTOBER 1964 THE AVILATION INVESTORS COMPANY OF FORT
LAUDERNALE, FLORIDA, RECEIVED AN INQUIRY ABOUT THE FOSISIBILITY OF BUYING A
C-119 AIRCRAFT FOR THE COLONBLAN GOVERNMENT. THE CALL WAS MADE BY RAYMOND
(NOT FURTHER IDENTIFIED) TO SAUDERS V. ROBERSON, AN AVILATION INVESTORS COMPANY
EMPLOYEE, WHO AGREED TO INVESTIGATE THE PROPOSED AIRCRAFT PURCHASE.
2. ON 5 OCTOBER ROBERSON RECEIVED A TELEPHONE CALL FROM A MAN WHO
IDENTIFIED HENSELY AS "RASH" (PHONETIC) REARLING THE POSSIBLE PURCHASE OF A
-51 AIRCRAFT OSENSELBY FOR THE COLONBLAN GOVERNMENT, BUT IT WAS ACTUALLY
INTENDED FOR HAITI. ROBERSON AGREED TO MEET WITH "RASIN" AT THE CONORES
BUTLING IN MIAMI TO DISCUSS DETAILS OF BOTH PURCHASES.
